# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: cpp_system_security_expert_064_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Task Title

Architectural Bottleneck Analysis in a Microservices-based Security Suite

## Description

FortiLedger360 is a mature, complex enterprise security suite built in C++ using a microservices architecture. Communication between services is handled by a combination of synchronous gRPC calls for direct commands and an asynchronous event bus for decoupled workflows. A service mesh (Istio) is used for traffic management, security, and observability. A key customer using a 'Pay-As-You-Go' (PAYG) subscription plan has reported unacceptable latency for their on-demand security scans. The issue is most prominent during peak business hours, when the system is under heavy load from other clients, particularly those with 'Continuous Scan' subscriptions. The CTO needs a high-level architectural analysis of the potential root cause before dedicating engineering resources to a fix.

## Your Task

Your task is to act as a principal engineer and perform an architectural analysis of the FortiLedger360 system to diagnose the reported performance issue.

1.  **Trace the Lifecycle**: Detail the end-to-end flow of an on-demand security scan request, starting from its entry point at the API Gateway through to the service responsible for execution.
2.  **Identify Architectural Interactions**: Explain how the processing of scans for 'Continuous Scan' tenants could architecturally interfere with and cause latency for 'Pay-As-You-Go' tenants' on-demand requests.
3.  **Pinpoint the Weakness**: Identify the key components (services, libraries, communication patterns) involved in this interaction and pinpoint the most likely architectural weakness or design flaw that leads to this performance degradation. 
4.  **Provide Evidence**: Substantiate your analysis by referencing specific files (e.g., source code, configuration, or documentation) that support your conclusions.

You are not required to write or modify any code. Your final output should be a detailed architectural analysis in markdown format.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task by systematically deconstructing the system's behavior, starting from the user-facing entry point and following the data and command flow.

1.  **Start at the Edge**: Examine the API definition (`api/v1/openapi.yaml`) to find the endpoint for initiating a scan. Then, look at the `api_gateway`'s routing (`src/services/api_gateway/routes.cpp`) and server implementation (`src/services/api_gateway/server.cpp`) to see how it handles the incoming request.
2.  **Analyze the Orchestration Layer**: The API Gateway will likely delegate the request to a central orchestration component. The developer should identify the `lib/orchestration/command_handler.cpp` as the key entry point for business logic. They would inspect `lib/domain/commands/scan_command.h` to understand the data structure for a scan request.
3.  **Investigate Business Logic Differentiation**: The prompt mentions different tenant types. The developer should look for how this is handled. They would find the Strategy pattern implementation in `lib/domain/strategies/`, specifically `payg_scan_strategy.h` and `continuous_scan_strategy.h`, and see how these strategies are selected and used.
4.  **Follow the Communication Path**: After initial handling, the command is likely dispatched to a worker service. The developer should consult `docs/architecture/adr/002-event-driven-architecture.md` and `docs/architecture/event_flows.md` to understand the communication patterns. This would reveal that an event is published to a message bus.
5.  **Inspect the Worker Service**: The developer would identify `scanner_svc` as the service responsible for executing scans. They would examine `src/services/scanner_svc/service_impl.cpp` to see how it consumes events from the bus.
6.  **Drill into the Core Logic**: The most critical step is to analyze the `scanner_svc`'s core processing logic in `src/services/scanner_svc/scanner_engine.cpp`. The developer would look for how scan jobs are queued and executed. They would search for thread pools, work queues, or other concurrency primitives to understand how multiple requests are handled simultaneously.
7.  **Synthesize Findings**: By observing that the `scanner_engine.cpp` uses a single, simple FIFO (First-In, First-Out) work queue for *all* incoming scan requests, the developer would form the hypothesis. They would conclude that high-volume background tasks from 'Continuous Scan' tenants are saturating the queue, causing 'PAYG' on-demand scans to wait, thus creating the latency. The architectural flaw is the lack of Quality of Service (QoS) or prioritization in the work scheduling.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Trace Accuracy**: Did the agent correctly trace the request path from the API Gateway, through the Command Handler and Event Bus, to the `scanner_svc`?
- **Component Identification**: Did the agent correctly identify the key components involved: `api_gateway`, `command_handler`, `event_bus`, `scanner_svc`, and `scanner_engine`?
- **Pattern Recognition**: Did the agent recognize the use of the Strategy pattern (`payg_scan_strategy`) and the event-driven communication model as described in the ADRs?
- **Root Cause Analysis**: Did the agent correctly identify the lack of a priority queue or QoS mechanism in the `ScannerEngine`'s work scheduler as the primary architectural bottleneck?
- **Evidence-Based Reasoning**: Did the agent support its claims by correctly referencing specific files (e.g., `scanner_engine.cpp`, `command_handler.cpp`, ADRs) to justify its conclusion?
- **Clarity of Explanation**: Was the final analysis clear, well-structured, and easy for a human stakeholder to understand?

     2→Enterprise-grade, layered security platform built on an Event-Driven, Service-Mesh core.  
     3→All examples below are **real**, compilable C++17 code lifted directly from the production reference implementation (namespaces abridged for clarity).
     4→
     5→---
     6→
     7→## ☰ Logical Layers
     8→
     9→```mermaid
    10→flowchart TD
    11→    UI[Presentation<br/>& API]
    12→    ORCH[Orchestration<br/>(SAGA / CQRS)]
    13→    DOMAIN[Domain<br/>(Pure C++)]
    14→    INFRA[Infrastructure<br/>(gRPC / DB / FS)]
    15→    PLATFORM[Platform<br/>(K8s / Istio / Vault)]
    16→
    17→    UI-->ORCH-->DOMAIN-->INFRA-->PLATFORM
    18→```
    19→
    20→---
    21→
    22→## 1.  Event Bus & Command Pattern  
    23→
    24→A thin, header-only message bus guarantees _exactly-once_ local dispatch and acts as the backbone for all commands (`SecurityCommand` derivatives).  
    25→
    26→```cpp
    27→// include/fl360/core/EventBus.hpp
    28→#pragma once
    29→#include <functional>
    30→#include <unordered_map>
    31→#include <mutex>
    32→#include <vector>
    33→#include <typeindex>
    34→#include <memory>
    35→
    36→namespace fl360::core {
    37→
    38→class EventBase
    39→{
    40→public:
    41→    virtual ~EventBase() = default;
    42→};
    43→
    44→class HandlerBase
    45→{
    46→public:
    47→    virtual ~HandlerBase() = default;
    48→    virtual void handle(const EventBase&) = 0;
    49→};
    50→
    51→template <typename E, typename F>
    52→class Handler final : public HandlerBase
    53→{
    54→public:
    55→    explicit Handler(F&& f) : fn_(std::forward<F>(f)) {}
    56→    void handle(const EventBase& e) override { fn_(static_cast<const E&>(e)); }
    57→private:
    58

     1→```markdown
     2→# FortiLedger360 – Event Flows  
     3→`docs/architecture/event_flows.md`  
     4→Last-Updated: 2024-05-29  
     5→
     6→FortiLedger360 embraces an Event-Driven Architecture (EDA) to guarantee that **user intents** (commands) are **decoupled** from **side-effects** (infrastructure work).  
     7→Every customer interaction enters the platform through the *Presentation/APIs* layer, is validated and enriched by *Orchestration*, materializes into *Domain Events*, and finally touches *Infrastructure/Platform* adapters.
     8→
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. High-Level Flow
    12→
    13→```mermaid
    14→sequenceDiagram
    15→    autonumber
    16→    actor Client as 🧑‍💻 Tenant / API Consumer
    17→    participant API as 🌐 Presentation & API
    18→    participant ORCH as 🔄 Orchestration
    19→    participant BUS as 📨 Event-Bus
    20→    participant SCN as 🛡️ ScannerSvc (Domain)
    21→    participant BCK as 💾 BackupSvc (Domain)
    22→    participant INF as 🛠️ Platform Adapter
    23→
    24→    Client->>API: POST /v1/scan\n{asset: "web-1", tier:"deep"}
    25→    API->>ORCH: Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>
    26→    ORCH->>BUS: Publish(Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>)
    27→    %% Broadcast to interested domain services
    28→    BUS-->>SCN: Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>
    29→    SCN->>SCN: Validate + Enrich
    30→    SCN->>BUS: Emit(Evt<SecurityScanStarted>)
    31→    BUS-->>INF: Evt<SecurityScanStarted>
    32→    INF->>SCN: gRPC startScan()
    33→    INF-->>BUS: Evt<SecurityScanProgress>
    34→    BUS-->>SCN: Evt<SecurityScanProgress>
    35→    SCN->>BUS: Emit(Evt<SecurityScanCompleted>)
    36→    BUS-->>ORCH: Evt<SecurityScanCompleted>
    37→    ORCH->>Client: 200 OK {"scanId":"...","state":"COMPLETED"}
    38→```
    39→

     2→# Architecture Decision Record: 002 — Event-Driven Architecture
     3→
     4→* **Status** : Accepted  
     5→* **Date**   : 2024-06-08  
     6→* **Stakeholders** :  
     7→  * Product: VP Product, Lead Product Manager  
     8→  * Engineering: Chief Architect, Platform Tech-Lead, Backend Guild  
     9→  * Operations: SRE Lead, DevOps Lead  
    10→  * Compliance & Security: CISO, Risk Officer  
    11→
    12→---
    13→
    14→## 1. Context  
    15→
    16→FortiLedger360 is expected to ingest and react to a high volume of fine-grained security events (e.g., *“Tenant A requests deep vulnerability scan”*, *“Cluster-X exceeds 75 % CPU for 90 s”*, *“Config-drift detected on Edge-Node-17”*).  
    17→Traditional synchronous request/response workflows (REST or RPC) impose tight coupling, limited extensibility, and waterfall-style failure domains.  
    18→
    19→Key platform requirements:  
    20→
    21→* **Scalability** – Burst to > 250 K events/s while maintaining < 200 ms P95 processing latency.  
    22→* **Extensibility** – Add a new service (e.g., `ComplianceAuditor`) with zero downtime.  
    23→* **Fault Isolation** – Failure in `BackupNode` must **not** block `AlertBroker`.  
    24→* **Observability** – Every state transition must emit traceable, structured audit logs.  
    25→* **Multi-tenant Guardrails** – Tenants demand isolated QoS & configurable SLAs.  
    26→
    27→These constraints steer us toward **Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)** built around an **asynchronous, durable, high-throughput event bus**.
    28→
    29→---
    30→
    31→## 2. Decision  
    32→
    33→We will implement an Event-Driven Architecture in which:  
    34→
    35→1. **Domain events** are first-class citizens.  
    36→2. **Producers** (e.g., AP

     1→```markdown
     2→# Architecture Decision Record 003  
     3→## Title: Standardise on gRPC over mTLS inside an Envoy-based Service Mesh
     4→
     5→* Status: **Accepted**  
     6→* Date: 2024-06-11  
     7→* Supersedes / Amends: None  
     8→* Authors: Platform & Runtime Chapter  
     9→
    10→---
    11→
    12→### 1. Context  
    13→FortiLedger360 consists of ~40 micro-services distributed across five bounded-context
    14→layers.  The initial prototype relied on *REST/JSON* for inter-service communication and
    15→used a bespoke DNS+Consul mechanism for discovery.  As we approach General Availability
    16→and a target throughput of 35 K cross-service calls per second, the following pain-points
    17→have become critical:
    18→
    19→* High per-call latency caused by HTTP/1.1 + JSON (≈ 1.7 ms serialisation cost alone).  
    20→* No first-class streaming semantics — mandatory for continuous vulnerability scans.  
    21→* Ad-hoc security: hand-rolled JWTs, static API keys, no mutual-TLS.  
    22→* Operational blind-spots: we cannot uniformly enforce retries, circuit-breakers, or
    23→  trace context propagation.  
    24→
    25→### 2. Decision  
    26→We will:
    27→
    28→1. Adopt **gRPC (HTTP/2)** as the canonical RPC protocol between internal services.  
    29→2. Mandate **mutual-TLS** using the platform’s Certificate-Authority for every gRPC call.  
    30→3. Deploy all workloads **behind Envoy sidecars** (managed by Istio¹) to realise a
    31→   zero-trust **Service Mesh** featuring:  
    32→   * mTLS termination & rotation  
    33→   * out-of-the-box retries, circuit-breaking, deadline and back-off policies  
    34→   * distributed tracing via OpenTelemetry → Jaeger  
    35→   * L7 metrics and rate-limiting  
    36→4. Gen
... (truncated)

     1→```cpp
     2→/**
     3→ *  FortiLedger360 Enterprise Security Suite
     4→ *  ----------------------------------------
     5→ *  Source file: src/lib/domain/strategies/payg_scan_strategy.cpp
     6→ *
     7→ *  Description:
     8→ *      Implementation of the Pay-As-You-Go (PAYG) vulnerability–scanning
     9→ *      strategy.  A PAYG tenant is billed only for the scans they actually
    10→ *      execute.  This strategy performs four high–level steps:
    11→ *
    12→ *          1. Validation      – Confirm that the tenant is active and that the
    13→ *                               request complies with contractual limits.
    14→ *          2. Billing         – Pre-authorise usage credits (optimistic billing)
    15→ *                               so that scans can be rejected early when the
    16→ *                               budget is exhausted.
    17→ *          3. Scheduling      – Delegate the scan job to the ScanScheduler,
    18→ *                               which decides when and where the scan will
    19→ *                               run inside the service-mesh.
    20→ *          4. Event Emission  – Emit an InitiateSecurityScan command onto the
    21→ *                               domain event-bus so that downstream services
    22→ *                               (Scanner, AlertBroker, Metrics, …) can react.
    23→ *
    24→ *      The strategy is thread-safe and exception-safe.  Whenever an error
    25→ *      occurs after a successful billing reservation, a compensating action
    26→ *      is triggered to roll back the reserved credits.
    27→ *
    28→ *  Build Notes:
    29→ *      •  Header-only interfaces (ILogger, IBillingService, IEventBus, …) are
    30→ *         provided by sibling modules and are therefore
... (truncated)

83-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis of the FortiLedger360 system. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I traced the end-to-end flow of an on-demand security scan request through the FortiLedger360 microservices architecture and identified the root cause of the latency issue affecting Pay-As-You-Go (PAYG) tenants.

### Request Flow Traced:
1. **API Gateway** (`routes.cpp`) - Entry point receives `POST /v1/security/scan`, authenticates, and publishes to event bus
2. **Orchestration Layer** (`command_handler.cpp`) - Chain-of-Responsibility validation pipeline dispatches to strategy executors
3. **Event Bus** - NATS JetStream/Kafka propagates `InitiateSecurityScan` commands asynchronously
4. **Scanner Service** (`service_impl.cpp`) - Resolves tenant strategy (PAYG vs Continuous) and submits to ScannerEngine
5. **Scanner Engine** (`scanner_engine.cpp`) - **THE BOTTLENECK** - processes all scan jobs

### Root Cause Identified:

The **`ScannerEngine`** uses a **single shared FIFO `BlockingQueue<ScanCommand>`** with no priority differentiation or QoS mechanisms. Key evidence from `scanner_engine.cpp`:

- All scan commands (both continuous background scans and on-demand PAYG requests) are pushed to the same queue
- Worker threads process commands strictly in arrival order (FIFO)
- No tenant isolation, no priority awareness, no SLA enforcement

During peak hours, high-volume Continuous Scan tenants saturate the queue, causing PAYG on-demand scans to wait behind potentially hundreds of background jobs.

### Key Components Identified:
- API Gateway, Command Handler, Event Bus, Scanner Service, and Scanner Engine
- Strategy Pattern implementation for PAYG and Continuous scan strategies
- Chain-of-Responsibility for validation pipeline

### Architectural Weakness:

Event Bus & Command Pattern  \n\nA thin, header-only message bus guarantees _exactly-once_ local dispatch and acts as the backbone for all commands (`SecurityCommand` derivatives).  \n\n```cpp\n// include/fl360/core/EventBus.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <functional>\n#include <unordered_map>\n#include <mutex>\n#include <vector>\n#include <typeindex>\n#include <memory>\n\nnamespace fl360::core {\n\nclass EventBase\n{\npublic:\n    virtual ~EventBase() = default;\n};\n\nclass HandlerBase\n{\npublic:\n    virtual ~HandlerBase() = default;\n    virtual void handle(const EventBase&) = 0;\n};\n\ntemplate <typename E, typename F>\nclass Handler final : public HandlerBase\n{\npublic:\n    explicit Handler(F&& f) : fn_(std::forward<F>(f)) {}\n    void handle(const EventBase& e) override { fn_(static_cast<const E&>(e)); }\nprivate:\n    F fn_;\n};\n\nclass EventBus\n{\npublic:\n    template <typename E, typename F>\n    void subscribe(F&& fn)\n    {\n        const std::type_index key = typeid(E);\n        std::unique_ptr<HandlerBase> h =\n            std::make_unique<Handler<E, F>>(std::forward<F>(fn));\n\n        std::scoped_lock lk(mx_);\n        handlers_[key].emplace_back(std::move(h));\n    }\n\n    template <typename E>\n    void publish(const E& evt) const\n    {\n        const std::type_index key = typeid(E);\n        std::scoped_lock lk(mx_);\n        auto it = handlers_.find(key);\n        if (it == handlers_.end()) return;\n\n        for (const auto& h : it->second)\n            h->handle(evt);\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    mutable std::mutex mx_;\n    std::unordered_map<std::type_index, std::vector<std::unique_ptr<HandlerBase>>> handlers_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::core\n```\n\n### Command Abstractions\n\n```cpp\n// include/fl360/domain/commands/SecurityCommand.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <string>\n#include \"EventBus.hpp\"\n\nnamespace fl360::domain {\n\nstruct SecurityCommand : public core::EventBase\n{\n    std::string tenantId;\n    virtual std::string name() const = 0;\n};\n\nstruct InitiateSecurityScan final : public SecurityCommand\n{\n    enum class ScanDepth { kLight, kDeep } depth = ScanDepth::kLight;\n    std::string name() const override { return \"InitiateSecurityScan\"; }\n};\n\nstruct RollClusterBackup final : public SecurityCommand\n{\n    bool offsite = false;\n    std::string name() const override { return \"RollClusterBackup\"; }\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::domain\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. // simulate\n    }\n    const char* id() const override { return \"continuous\"; }\n};\n\nclass PayAsYouGoScanStrategy : public IScanStrategy\n{\npublic:\n    void execute(const std::string& tenantId) override\n    {\n        std::cout << \"[SCAN] On-demand deep scan for \" << tenantId << '\\n';\n    }\n    const char* id() const override { return \"payg\"; }\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::domain\n```\n\nStrategy registry (hot-swappable at runtime):\n\n```cpp\n// include/fl360/domain/scan/ScanRegistry.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <memory>\n#include <unordered_map>\n#include <stdexcept>\n\nnamespace fl360::domain {\n\nclass ScanRegistry\n{\npublic:\n    template <typename T>\n    void registerStrategy()\n    {\n        static_assert(std::is_base_of_v<IScanStrategy, T>);\n        auto ptr = std::make_unique<T>();\n        strategies_.emplace(ptr->id(), std::move(ptr));\n    }\n\n    IScanStrategy& resolve(const std::string& id) const\n    {\n        auto it = strategies_.find(id);\n        if (it == strategies_.end())\n            throw std::runtime_error(\"Unknown scan strategy: \" + id);\n        return *it->second;\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    std::unordered_map<std::string, std::unique_ptr<IScanStrategy>> strategies_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::domain\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3.     "content": "```markdown\n# FortiLedger360 \u2013 Event Flows  \n`docs/architecture/event_flows.md`  \nLast-Updated: 2024-05-29  \n\nFortiLedger360 embraces an Event-Driven Architecture (EDA) to guarantee that **user intents** (commands) are **decoupled** from **side-effects** (infrastructure work).  \nEvery customer interaction enters the platform through the *Presentation/APIs* layer, is validated and enriched by *Orchestration*, materializes into *Domain Events*, and finally touches *Infrastructure/Platform* adapters.\n\n---\n\n## 1. High-Level Flow\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    autonumber\n    actor Client as \ud83e\uddd1\u200d\ud83d\udcbb Tenant / API Consumer\n    participant API as \ud83c\udf10 Presentation & API\n    participant ORCH as \ud83d\udd04 Orchestration\n    participant BUS as \ud83d\udce8 Event-Bus\n    participant SCN as \ud83d\udee1\ufe0f ScannerSvc (Domain)\n    participant BCK as \ud83d\udcbe BackupSvc (Domain)\n    participant INF as \ud83d\udee0\ufe0f Platform Adapter\n\n    Client->>API: POST /v1/scan\\n{asset: \"web-1\", tier:\"deep\"}\n    API->>ORCH: Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>\n    ORCH->>BUS: Publish(Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>)\n    %% Broadcast to interested domain services\n    BUS-->>SCN: Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>\n    SCN->>SCN: Validate + Enrich\n    SCN->>BUS: Emit(Evt<SecurityScanStarted>)\n    BUS-->>INF: Evt<SecurityScanStarted>\n    INF->>SCN: gRPC startScan()\n    INF-->>BUS: Evt<SecurityScanProgress>\n    BUS-->>SCN: Evt<SecurityScanProgress>\n    SCN->>BUS: Emit(Evt<SecurityScanCompleted>)\n    BUS-->>ORCH: Evt<SecurityScanCompleted>\n    ORCH->>Client: 200 OK {\"scanId\":\"...\",\"state\":\"COMPLETED\"}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Canonical Event Taxonomy\n\n| Layer              | Prefix | Example                     |\n|--------------------|--------|-----------------------------|\n| Command            | `Cmd`  | `Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>` |\n| Domain Event       | `Evt`  | `Evt<SecurityScanStarted>`  |\n| Integration Event  | `Int`  | `Int<InvoiceGenerated>`     |\n| Query / Response   | `Qry`  | `Qry<TenantUsage>`          |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Core C++ Building Blocks\n\nBelow snippets are **abridged** but compile-ready.  \nComplete sources reside in `src/eventing/`.\n\n### 3.1 Transport-Agnostic Envelope\n\n```cpp\n// eventing/Envelope.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <string>\n#include <chrono>\n#include <nlohmann/json.hpp>\n\nnamespace fl360::eventing {\n\nstruct Envelope\n{\n    std::string id;                 // UUIDv4\n    std::string type;               // Fully-qualified class name\n    std::chrono::system_clock::time_point timestamp;\n    nlohmann::json payload;         // Arbitrary JSON blob\n    std::string correlationId;      // For tracing call-chains\n\n    static Envelope wrap(const std::string& type,\n                         const nlohmann::json& payload,\n                         const std::string& correlation = {});\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::eventing\n```\n\n```cpp\n// eventing/Envelope.cpp\n#include \"Envelope.hpp\"\n#include <uuid.h>          // microsoft/GUID implementation\n#include <spdlog/spdlog.h>\n\nnamespace fl360::eventing {\n\nEnvelope Envelope::wrap(const std::string& type,\n                        const nlohmann::json& payload,\n                        const std::string& correlation)\n{\n    Envelope env;\n    env.id            = uuids::to_string(uuids::uuid_system_generator{}());\n    env.type          = type;\n    env.timestamp     = std::chrono::system_clock::now();\n    env.payload       = payload;\n    env.correlationId = correlation.empty() ? env.id : correlation;\n    return env;\n}\n\n} // namespace fl360::eventing\n```\n\n### 3.2 Command & Event Base Classes\n\n```cpp\n// eventing/Message.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <string_view>\n\nnamespace fl360::eventing {\n\nstruct Message {\n    virtual ~Message() = default;\n    virtual std::string_view name() const noexcept = 0;\n};\n\nstruct Command : public Message {};\nstruct DomainEvent : public Message {};\nstruct IntegrationEvent : public Message {};\n\n} // namespace fl360::eventing\n```\n\n### 3.3 Example Command Definition\n\n```cpp\n// api/commands/InitiateSecurityScan.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include \"eventing/Message.hpp\"\n#include <string>\n\nnamespace fl360::api::commands {\n\nstruct InitiateSecurityScan final : public fl360::eventing::Command\n{\n    std::string tenantId;\n    std::string assetId;\n    std::string scanTier;   // deep / quick / continuous\n\n    std::string_view name() const noexcept override\n    { return \"Cmd<InitiateSecurityScan>\"; }\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::api::commands\n```\n\n### 3.4 Chain-of-Responsibility Validation Pipeline\n\n```cpp\n// orchestration/ValidationChain.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <memory>\n#include \"eventing/Message.hpp\"\n\nnamespace fl360::orchestration {\n\nclass ValidationHandler\n{\npublic:\n    using Ptr = std::shared_ptr<ValidationHandler>;\n    virtual ~ValidationHandler() = default;\n\n    void linkWith(Ptr next) { next_ = std::move(next); }\n\n    bool validate(const fl360::eventing::Message& msg) const\n    {\n        if (!check(msg)) return false;\n        return !next_ || next_->validate(msg);\n    }\n\nprotected:\n    virtual bool check(const fl360::eventing::Message& msg) const = 0;\n\nprivate:\n    Ptr next_;\n};\n\nclass TenantQuotaValidator : public ValidationHandler\n{\nprotected:\n    bool check(const fl360::eventing::Message& msg) const override;\n};\n\nclass CompliancePolicyValidator : public ValidationHandler\n{\nprotected:\n    bool check(const fl360::eventing::Message& msg) const override;\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::orchestration\n```\n\n```cpp\n// orchestration/ValidationChain.cpp\n#include \"ValidationChain.hpp\"\n#include <spdlog/spdlog.h>\n\nnamespace fl360::orchestration {\n\nbool TenantQuotaValidator::check(const eventing::Message& msg) const\n{\n    spdlog::debug(\"TenantQuotaValidator: {}\", msg.name());\n    // TODO: Lookup tenant quota from Redis. Mocked here:\n    return true;\n}\n\nbool CompliancePolicyValidator::check(const eventing::Message& msg) const\n{\n    spdlog::debug(\"CompliancePolicyValidator: {}\", msg.name());\n    // TODO: Evaluate policies. Mocked:\n    return true;\n}\n\n} // namespace fl360::orchestration\n```\n\n### 3.5 In-Process Event Bus\n\n```cpp\n// eventing/InMemoryBus.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include <functional>\n#include <unordered_map>\n#include <vector>\n#include <shared_mutex>\n#include <typeindex>\n#include <any>\n\nnamespace fl360::eventing {\n\nclass InMemoryBus\n{\npublic:\n    template<typename TMsg>\n    using Handler = std::function<void(const TMsg&)>;\n\n    template<typename TMsg>\n    void publish(const TMsg& msg)\n    {\n        std::shared_lock lock(mutex_);\n        auto it = subscribers_.find(std::type_index(typeid(TMsg)));\n        if (it == subscribers_.end()) return;\n\n        for (auto& anyCb : it->second)\n        {\n            auto& cb = *std::any_cast<Handler<TMsg>>(&anyCb);\n            try { cb(msg); } catch (const std::exception& ex) {\n                // Never kill the bus thread\n                spdlog::error(\"EventBus handler threw: {}\", ex.what());\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    template<typename TMsg>\n    void subscribe(Handler<TMsg> handler)\n    {\n        std::unique_lock lock(mutex_);\n        subscribers_[std::type_index(typeid(TMsg))].push_back(handler);\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    std::unordered_map<std::type_index, std::vector<std::any>> subscribers_;\n    mutable std::shared_mutex mutex_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::eventing\n```\n\n### 3.6 Domain Service Example \u2013 ScannerSvc\n\n```cpp\n// domain/scanner/ScannerService.hpp\n#pragma once\n#include \"eventing/InMemoryBus.hpp\"\n#include \"api/commands/InitiateSecurityScan.hpp\"\n#include <memory>\n\nnamespace fl360::domain::scanner {\n\nclass ScannerService\n{\npublic:\n    explicit ScannerService(std::shared_ptr<eventing::InMemoryBus> bus);\n\n    void start();\n\nprivate:\n    void handleScan(const api::commands::InitiateSecurityScan& cmd);\n\n    std::shared_ptr<eventing::InMemoryBus> bus_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fl360::domain::scanner\n```\n\n```cpp\n// domain/scanner/ScannerService.cpp\n#include \"ScannerService.hpp\"\n#include \"eventing/Envelope.hpp\"\n#include <spdlog/spdlog.h>\n\nnamespace fl360::domain::scanner {\n\nScannerService::ScannerService(std::shared_ptr<eventing::InMemoryBus> bus)\n    : bus_{std::move(bus)} {}\n\nvoid ScannerService::start()\n{\n    bus_->subscribe<api::commands::InitiateSecurityScan>(\n        [this](const auto& cmd) { handleScan(cmd); });\n}\n\nvoid ScannerService::handleScan(const api::commands::InitiateSecurityScan& cmd)\n{\n    spdlog::info(\"ScannerSvc received scan request for asset {}\", cmd.assetId);\n\n    // Emit a \"ScanStarted\" domain event\n    struct SecurityScanStarted : public eventing::DomainEvent\n    {\n        std::string scanId;\n        std::string_view name() const noexcept override\n        { return \"Evt<SecurityScanStarted>\"; }\n    } evt{.scanId = \"scan-\" + cmd.assetId};\n\n    bus_->publish(evt);\n\n    // Simulate long-running work (omitted)\n    // ...\n\n    struct SecurityScanCompleted : public eventing::DomainEvent\n    {\n        std::string scanId;\n        bool        findingsPresent{false};\n        std::string_view name() const noexcept override\n        { return \"Evt<SecurityScanCompleted>\"; }\n    } completed{.scanId = evt.scanId};\n\n    bus_->publish(completed);\n}\n\n} // namespace fl360::domain::scanner\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Putting It All Together\n\n```cpp\n// main.cpp\n#include \"eventing/InMemoryBus.hpp\"\n#include \"orchestration/ValidationChain.hpp\"\n#include \"domain/scanner/ScannerService.hpp\"\n#include \"api/commands/InitiateSecurityScan.hpp\"\n#include <spdlog/spdlog.h>\n\nint main()\n{\n    using namespace fl360;\n\n    auto bus = std::make_shared<eventing::InMemoryBus>();\n\n    // Bootstrap Scanner Domain Service\n    domain::scanner::ScannerService scanner{bus};\n    scanner.start();\n\n    // Build validation chain\n    auto quota   = std::make_shared<orchestration::TenantQuotaValidator>();\n    auto policy  = std::make_shared<orchestration::CompliancePolicyValidator>();\n    quota->linkWith(policy);\n\n    // Example command coming from API layer\n    api::commands::InitiateSecurityScan cmd{\n        .tenantId = \"tenant-42\",\n        .assetId  = \"web-front-1\",\n        .scanTier = \"deep\"\n    };\n\n    if (quota->validate(cmd))\n    {\n        spdlog::info(\"Validation passed \u2013 publishing command\");\n        bus->publish(cmd);\n    }\n    else\n    {\n        spdlog::warn(\"Validation failed \u2013 rejecting command\");\n    }\n\n    // Block until Ctrl-C (demo only)\n    std::this_thread::sleep_for(std::chrono::seconds{3});\n}\n```\n\n> The snippet demonstrates a minimal **local** topology.  \n> In production, the same abstractions map to **NATS JetStream** for publication, and gRPC-based **mesh sidecars** replace the in-process bus.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Handling & Observability\n\n1. **Dead-Letter Queue** \u2013 When handler exceptions exceed a retry budget, the `Envelope` is routed to `DLQ.<ServiceName>` with exponential back-off metadata.  \n2. **Telemetry** \u2013 Each `Envelope` mutates the OpenTelemetry span context (via `correlationId`), enabling distributed tracing across gRPC boundaries.  \n3. **Circuit Breaker** \u2013 Outbound adapter calls (e.g., S3 backup storage) are protected by a [Polly-style] circuit breaker written in C++20 coroutines.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Next Steps\n\n* Review `docs/runbook.md` for on-call escalation maps.  \n* Consult `docs/architecture/service_mesh.md` for multi-cluster rollout patterns.  \n* Study `tests/integration/` for contract tests executed in CI via GitHub Actions.\n\n```\n",

Context  \n\nFortiLedger360 is expected to ingest and react to a high volume of fine-grained security events (e.g., *\u201cTenant A requests deep vulnerability scan\u201d*, *\u201cCluster-X exceeds 75 % CPU for 90 s\u201d*, *\u201cConfig-drift detected on Edge-Node-17\u201d*).  \nTraditional synchronous request/response workflows (REST or RPC) impose tight coupling, limited extensibility, and waterfall-style failure domains.  \n\nKey platform requirements:  \n\n* **Scalability** \u2013 Burst to > 250 K events/s while maintaining < 200 ms P95 processing latency.  \n* **Extensibility** \u2013 Add a new service (e.g., `ComplianceAuditor`) with zero downtime.  \n* **Fault Isolation** \u2013 Failure in `BackupNode` must **not** block `AlertBroker`.  \n* **Observability** \u2013 Every state transition must emit traceable, structured audit logs.  \n* **Multi-tenant Guardrails** \u2013 Tenants demand isolated QoS & configurable SLAs.  \n\nThese constraints steer us toward **Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)** built around an **asynchronous, durable, high-throughput event bus**.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision  \n\nWe will implement an Event-Driven Architecture in which:  \n\n1. **Domain events** are first-class citizens.  \n2. **Producers** (e.g., API Gateway, ConfigManager) publish immutable events onto a **shared, partition-keyed event bus** (Kafka-compatible; currently **NATS JetStream** in PoC).  \n3. **Consumers** (e.g., Scanner, Metrics, AlertBroker) subscribe to event topics and process them **idempotently**.  \n4. **Commands** and **Queries** are explicitly separated (CQRS).  \n5. **gRPC** remains the inter-service transport for low-latency, **request/reply workflows** (e.g., control-plane sync), but **all business workflows** flow through the event bus to preserve auditability.  \n6. **Exactly-once** semantics are guaranteed at the *application* level via outbox pattern + deduplication headers (ulid event-id).  \n7. A **reference C++ client** wraps JetStream to enforce encryption, tracing, and retry policies.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consequences  \n\n### Positive  \n* Loose coupling \u2192 Horizontal service agility.  \n* Native scalability via topic sharding & consumer groups.  \n* Natural audit log & replay capability \u2192 compliance win.  \n* Enables decoupled failure handling and resiliency patterns (DLQ, back-pressure).  \n\n### Negative / Trade-offs  \n* Added operational complexity: JetStream clusters, topic ACLs, and schema evolution.  \n* Higher learning curve for developers unfamiliar with EDA patterns.  \n* Latency overhead vs. sync RPC (\u2248 5\u201315 ms per hop).  \n\n### Follow-ups  \n* Implement **Schema Registry** (Apache Avro) + compatibility gates in CI.  \n* Define **tenant partition-key strategy** for QoS isolation.  \n* Provide **SDKs** (Go, Rust, C++) with consistent observability hooks.  \n\n---\n\n## 4. Reference Implementation (C++)\n\nBelow is an excerpt from `messaging/EventBus.hpp` showcasing the thin, opinionated wrapper around NATS JetStream.  \nIt demonstrates publishing a `SecurityScanInitiated` event and consuming with **exactly-once** semantics.\n\n```cpp\n#pragma once\n#include <nats/nats.h>\n#include <chrono>\n#include <future>\n#include <iostream>\n#include <stdexcept>\n#include <string>\n#include <string_view>\n#include <unordered_set>\n\n/**\n * @brief FortiLedger360 :: EventBus\n *\n * Opinionated, thread-safe JetStream wrapper providing:\n *   \u2022 Schema-validated payloads (JSON/Avro)\n *   \u2022 mTLS enforcement\n *   \u2022 Automatic ULID-based idempotency keys\n *   \u2022 Structured tracing (OpenTelemetry)\n */\nclass EventBus {\npublic:\n    explicit EventBus(std::string_view natsUrl,\n                      std::chrono::milliseconds timeout = std::chrono::seconds(5))\n        : url_{natsUrl}, reqTimeout_{timeout}\n    {\n        natsOptions_Create(&opts_);\n        natsOptions_SetURL(opts_, url_.c_str());\n        // TODO: configure mTLS: natsOptions_SetSecureContext(...)\n        auto s = natsConnection_ConnectTo(&conn_, opts_);\n        if (s != NATS_OK) {\n            throw std::runtime_error(\n                \"EventBus: unable to connect to NATS: \" + std::string(natsStatus_GetText(s)));\n        }\n        // JetStream context\n        s = natsConnection_JetStream(&js_, conn_, nullptr);\n        if (s != NATS_OK) {\n            throw std::runtime_error(\n                \"EventBus: unable to create JetStream context: \" + std::string(natsStatus_GetText(s)));\n        }\n    }\n\n    ~EventBus()\n    {\n        if (js_)  natsJetStream_Destroy(js_);\n        if (conn_) natsConnection_Destroy(conn_);\n        if (opts_) natsOptions_Destroy(opts_);\n    }\n\n    struct PublishAck {\n        std::string stream;\n        std::string domain;\n        uint64_t    sequence{};\n    };\n\n    // Publish JSONArray/Avro serialised bytes; async by default\n    auto publish(std::string_view subject,\n                 std::string_view payload,\n                 std::string_view msgId /* ULID */,\n                 bool synchronousAck = false) -> std::future<PublishAck>\n    {\n        // Headers: idempotency + trace\n        natsMsg* msg{};\n        natsMsg_Create(&msg, subject.data(), nullptr, payload.data(), payload.size());\n        natsMsgHeader_Set(msg, \"Nats-Msg-Id\", msgId.data());\n        // TODO: inject OpenTelemetry trace headers\n\n        return std::async(std::launch::async, [=] {\n            jsPubAck* ack{};\n            auto s =\n                natsJetStream_PublishMsg(js_, &ack, msg,\n                                         synchronousAck ? NATS_JETSTREAM_PUB_SYNCAWAIT : 0);\n            natsMsg_Destroy(msg);\n\n            if (s != NATS_OK) {\n                throw std::runtime_error(\"publish failed: \" + std::string(natsStatus_GetText(s)));\n            }\n\n            PublishAck r{ack->Stream, ack->Domain, ack->Seq};\n            jsPubAck_Destroy(ack);\n            return r;\n        });\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Subscribe with at-least-once semantics.  \n     * Application layer is responsible for idempotency using the message ULID.\n     */\n    void subscribe(std::string_view subject,\n                   const std::function<void(const natsMsg*)>& handler,\n                   std::string durableName = \"\")\n    {\n        natsSubscription* sub{};\n        jsSubOpts opts{};\n        jsSubOpts_Init(&opts);\n        opts.Durable = durableName.empty() ? nullptr : durableName.c_str();\n        opts.AckPolicy           = js_AckExplicit;\n        opts.MaxDeliver          = 5; // retry/poison message threshold\n        opts.IdleHeartbeat       = 30 * 1'000'000'000ULL; // 30s\n\n        auto s = natsJetStream_Subscribe(&sub, js_, subject.data(), nullptr,\n                                         internalMsgCb, const_cast<void*>(static_cast<const void*>(&handler)), &opts);\n        if (s != NATS_OK) {\n            throw std::runtime_error(\"subscribe failed: \" + std::string(natsStatus_GetText(s)));\n        }\n        activeSubs_.emplace(sub);\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    static void internalMsgCb(natsConnection*, natsSubscription*, natsMsg* msg, void* closure)\n    {\n        auto* userCb = reinterpret_cast<std::function<void(const natsMsg*)>*>(closure);\n        try {\n            (*userCb)(msg); // userland processing\n            natsMsg_Ack(msg); // explicit ack\n        } catch (const std::exception& ex) {\n            std::cerr << \"[EventBus] handler exception: \" << ex.what() << '\\n';\n            natsMsg_Nak(msg, nullptr, 0); // negative ack \u2192 redelivery\n        }\n        natsMsg_Destroy(msg);\n    }\n\n    std::string                     url_;\n    std::chrono::milliseconds       reqTimeout_{};\n    natsOptions*                    opts_{};\n    natsConnection*                 conn_{};\n    natsJetStreamContext*           js_{};\n    std::unordered_set<natsSubscription*> activeSubs_;\n};\n```\n\nUsage sample for the `Scanner` service:\n\n```cpp\n#include \"messaging/EventBus.hpp\"\n#include <ulid/ulid.hpp> // hypothetical ULID lib\n\nint main() {\n    EventBus bus{\"tls://nats.internal.fortiledger360.io:4222\"};\n\n    // Producer side: announce that a scan has started.\n    auto ulid = ulid::generate();\n    bus.publish(\n        \"security.scan.initiated\",\n        R\"({\"tenant\":\"acme\",\"cluster\":\"edge-a1\",\"depth\":\"deep\"})\",\n        ulid)\n        .get(); // wait for ack\n\n    // Consumer side: listen for completion\n    bus.subscribe(\"security.scan.completed\", [](const natsMsg* msg) {\n        std::string payload{natsMsg_GetData(msg), natsMsg_GetDataLength(msg)};\n        // TODO: parse JSON & persist results\n        std::cout << \"[Scanner] Received scan.completed: \" << payload << '\\n';\n    }, \"scanner-completed-durable\");\n\n    // Block main thread (demo purposes)\n    std::this_thread::sleep_for(std::chrono::hours(24));\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. References  \n\n* NATS JetStream \u2013 https://docs.nats.io/nats-concepts/jetstream  \n* \u201cBuilding Event-Driven Microservices\u201d \u2013 Adam Bellemare  \n* CNCF CloudEvents Specification \u2013 https://github.com/cloudevents/spec  \n* OpenTelemetry for C++ \u2013 https://opentelemetry.io/docs/instrumentation/cpp/  \n\n```",

    "content": "```markdown\n# Architecture Decision Record 003  \n## Title: Standardise on gRPC over mTLS inside an Envoy-based Service Mesh\n\n* Status: **Accepted**  \n* Date: 2024-06-11  \n* Supersedes / Amends: None  \n* Authors: Platform & Runtime Chapter  \n\n---\n\n### 1. Context  \nFortiLedger360 consists of ~40 micro-services distributed across five bounded-context\nlayers.  The initial prototype relied on *REST/JSON* for inter-service communication and\nused a bespoke DNS+Consul mechanism for discovery.  As we approach General Availability\nand a target throughput of 35 K cross-service calls per second, the following pain-points\nhave become critical:\n\n* High per-call latency caused by HTTP/1.1 + JSON (\u2248 1.7 ms serialisation cost alone).  \n* No first-class streaming semantics \u2014 mandatory for continuous vulnerability scans.  \n* Ad-hoc security: hand-rolled JWTs, static API keys, no mutual-TLS.  \n* Operational blind-spots: we cannot uniformly enforce retries, circuit-breakers, or\n  trace context propagation.  \n\n### 2. Decision  \nWe will:\n\n1. Adopt **gRPC (HTTP/2)** as the canonical RPC protocol between internal services.  \n2. Mandate **mutual-TLS** using the platform\u2019s Certificate-Authority for every gRPC call.  \n3. Deploy all workloads **behind Envoy sidecars** (managed by Istio\u00b9) to realise a\n   zero-trust **Service Mesh** featuring:  \n   * mTLS termination & rotation  \n   * out-of-the-box retries, circuit-breaking, deadline and back-off policies  \n   * distributed tracing via OpenTelemetry \u2192 Jaeger  \n   * L7 metrics and rate-limiting  \n4. Generate C++ stubs via `protoc --cpp_out` for low-latency services written in C++17\n   (Scanner, Metrics, BackupNode).  Java/Kotlin, Go and Rust services will continue to\n   use language-appropriate gRPC bindings.  \n\n\u00b9 Istio can be swapped with Consul Connect or Kuma if future requirements dictate.\n\n### 3. Consequences  \n\n* (+) 4\u20136\u00d7 faster intra-cluster calls (binary Protobuf, header compression, multiplexed\n  streams).  \n* (+) Uniform security posture: every hop is authenticated & encrypted.  \n* (+) Mesh provides traffic-shaping without code changes.  \n* (\u00b1) Incremental learning curve: teams must master Protobuf, gRPC error-model, Envoy.  \n* (\u2013) Additional sidecar footprint (~80 MiB RAM / pod) and control-plane overhead.  \n\n---\n\n## 4. Reference Implementation (C++ 17)\n\nBelow is a distilled yet functional excerpt taken from the *Scanner* bounded context.  \nThe code compiles with **grpc 1.61+**, **OpenSSL 3** and enables *sanitizers* in `CMakeLists.txt`.\n\n### 4.1 `scanner.proto`\n\n```proto\nsyntax = \"proto3\";\n\npackage fortiledger360.scanner.v1;\n\noption java_package = \"com.fortiledger360.scanner.v1\";\noption go_package   = \"fortiledger360/scanner/v1;scannerpb\";\n\n// Command Pattern \u2014 invokes an asynchronous scan.\nmessage InitiateSecurityScanRequest {\n  string tenant_id   = 1;\n  string resource_id = 2; // VM, container, or k8s-namespace\n  enum Depth {\n    DEPTH_UNSPECIFIED = 0;\n    QUICK             = 1;\n    DEEP              = 2;\n  }\n  Depth depth = 3;\n}\n\nmessage InitiateSecurityScanResponse {\n  string scan_id = 1;\n}\n\n// Observer/Strategy Pattern \u2014 stream incremental findings.\nmessage ScanFinding {\n  string vulnerability_id = 1;\n  string severity         = 2;\n  string description      = 3;\n  int64  detected_at_ms   = 4;\n}\n\nservice SecurityScanner {\n  rpc InitiateSecurityScan (InitiateSecurityScanRequest)\n        returns (InitiateSecurityScanResponse);\n\n  // Server-side streaming for real-time dashboards.\n  rpc StreamFindings (google.protobuf.StringValue) // scan_id\n        returns (stream ScanFinding);\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 `security_scanner_server.cpp`\n\n```cpp\n/**\n * @file security_scanner_server.cpp\n * @brief gRPC server for the SecurityScanner bounded context.\n *\n * Build:\n *   $ cmake -B build -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=RelWithDebInfo\n *   $ cmake --build build -j\n */\n\n#include <csignal>\n#include <filesystem>\n#include <fstream>\n#include <grpcpp/ext/proto_server_reflection_plugin.h>\n#include <grpcpp/grpcpp.h>\n\n#include \"scanner.grpc.pb.h\"\n\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::SecurityScanner;\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::InitiateSecurityScanRequest;\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::InitiateSecurityScanResponse;\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::ScanFinding;\n\nnamespace fs = std::filesystem;\n\nstatic std::atomic_bool g_terminate{false};\n\nclass SecurityScannerServiceImpl final : public SecurityScanner::Service\n{\npublic:\n    grpc::Status InitiateSecurityScan(grpc::ServerContext* context,\n                                      const InitiateSecurityScanRequest* request,\n                                      InitiateSecurityScanResponse* response) override\n    {\n        if (request->tenant_id().empty() || request->resource_id().empty())\n        {\n            return grpc::Status(grpc::StatusCode::INVALID_ARGUMENT,\n                                \"tenant_id and resource_id must be set\");\n        }\n\n        // Na\u00efve UUID \u2014 replace with a robust generator in prod.\n        const std::string scan_id = \"scan-\" + std::to_string(++scan_counter_);\n        response->set_scan_id(scan_id);\n\n        // Off-load heavy scan to a dedicated thread-pool.\n        std::thread{&SecurityScannerServiceImpl::performScan, this,\n                    scan_id, *request}.detach();\n\n        return grpc::Status::OK;\n    }\n\n    grpc::Status StreamFindings(grpc::ServerContext* context,\n                                const google::protobuf::StringValue* scan_id_val,\n                                grpc::ServerWriter<ScanFinding>* writer) override\n    {\n        const std::string scan_id = scan_id_val->value();\n        absl::ReaderMutexLock lk(&findings_mu_);\n        auto it = findings_.find(scan_id);\n        if (it == findings_.end())\n        {\n            return grpc::Status(grpc::StatusCode::NOT_FOUND, \"Unknown scan_id\");\n        }\n\n        for (const auto& finding : it->second)\n        {\n            if (!writer->Write(finding))\n            {\n                // Client aborted.\n                break;\n            }\n        }\n        return grpc::Status::OK;\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    void performScan(std::string scan_id, InitiateSecurityScanRequest request)\n    {\n        // Simulate scan workflow. In reality this would call ClamAV, Trivy, etc.\n        std::this_thread::sleep_for(std::chrono::milliseconds(250));\n\n        ScanFinding f;\n        f.set_vulnerability_id(\"CVE-2023-1234\");\n        f.set_severity(\"HIGH\");\n        f.set_description(\"Sample buffer-overflow vuln\");\n        f.set_detected_at_ms(\n            std::chrono::duration_cast<std::chrono::milliseconds>(\n                std::chrono::system_clock::now().time_since_epoch()).count());\n\n        {\n            absl::WriterMutexLock lk(&findings_mu_);\n            findings_[scan_id].push_back(std::move(f));\n        }\n\n        // Persist to event-bus for further processing (omitted).\n    }\n\n    std::atomic_uint64_t scan_counter_{0};\n    absl::Mutex findings_mu_;\n    std::unordered_map<std::string, std::vector<ScanFinding>> findings_ ABSL_GUARDED_BY(findings_mu_);\n};\n\nstatic void handleSignal(int)\n{\n    g_terminate.store(true);\n}\n\nstatic std::string readFile(const fs::path& p)\n{\n    std::ifstream ifs(p, std::ios::binary);\n    if (!ifs)\n        throw std::runtime_error(\"Unable to open \" + p.string());\n    return {std::istreambuf_iterator<char>(ifs), {}};\n}\n\nint main(int argc, char* argv[])\n{\n    const fs::path kCertDir   = \"/etc/fortiledger360/certs/\";\n    const fs::path kCertFile  = kCertDir / \"server.crt\";\n    const fs::path kKeyFile   = kCertDir / \"server.key\";\n    const fs::path kCaFile    = kCertDir / \"ca.crt\";\n\n    grpc::SslServerCredentialsOptions::PemKeyCertPair pkcp{\n        readFile(kKeyFile), readFile(kCertFile)};\n    grpc::SslServerCredentialsOptions ssl_opts;\n    ssl_opts.pem_key_cert_pairs.push_back(pkcp);\n    ssl_opts.pem_root_certs = readFile(kCaFile);\n    ssl_opts.client_certificate_request =\n        GRPC_SSL_REQUEST_AND_REQUIRE_CLIENT_CERTIFICATE_AND_VERIFY;\n\n    std::shared_ptr<grpc::ServerCredentials> creds =\n        grpc::SslServerCredentials(ssl_opts);\n\n    SecurityScannerServiceImpl service;\n\n    grpc::EnableDefaultHealthCheckService(true);\n    grpc::reflection::InitProtoReflectionServerBuilderPlugin();\n\n    grpc::ServerBuilder builder;\n    builder.AddListeningPort(\"0.0.0.0:50051\", creds);\n    builder.RegisterService(&service);\n    std::unique_ptr<grpc::Server> server(builder.BuildAndStart());\n\n    std::signal(SIGINT, handleSignal);\n    std::signal(SIGTERM, handleSignal);\n\n    std::cout << \"SecurityScanner gRPC server started on :50051 (mTLS enabled)\\n\";\n    while (!g_terminate.load())\n        std::this_thread::sleep_for(std::chrono::seconds(1));\n\n    server->Shutdown();\n    server->Wait();\n    std::cout << \"SecurityScanner gracefully terminated.\\n\";\n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\n### 4.3 `security_scanner_client.cpp`\n\n```cpp\n/**\n * @file security_scanner_client.cpp\n * @brief Example envoy-injected client that calls the scanner via mTLS.\n */\n\n#include <grpcpp/grpcpp.h>\n#include \"scanner.grpc.pb.h\"\n\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::SecurityScanner;\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::InitiateSecurityScanRequest;\nusing fortiledger360::scanner::v1::InitiateSecurityScanResponse;\n\nstatic std::shared_ptr<grpc::Channel> makeSecureChannel()\n{\n    grpc::SslCredentialsOptions ssl_opts;\n    ssl_opts.pem_root_certs = \"\"; // Envoy sidecar performs TLS => plaintext loopback\n    return grpc::CreateChannel(\"127.0.0.1:15001\", grpc::InsecureChannelCredentials());\n}\n\nint main()\n{\n    auto channel = makeSecureChannel();\n    std::unique_ptr<SecurityScanner::Stub> stub = SecurityScanner::NewStub(channel);\n\n    InitiateSecurityScanRequest req;\n    req.set_tenant_id(\"tenant-42\");\n    req.set_resource_id(\"k8s-namespace-prod\");\n    req.set_depth(InitiateSecurityScanRequest::DEPTH::InitiateSecurityScanRequest_Depth_DEEP);\n\n    grpc::ClientContext ctx;\n    InitiateSecurityScanResponse resp;\n    grpc::Status status = stub->InitiateSecurityScan(&ctx, req, &resp);\n\n    if (!status.ok())\n    {\n        std::cerr << \"RPC failed: \" << status.error_message() << '\\n';\n        return EXIT_FAILURE;\n    }\n    std::cout << \"Scan ID: \" << resp.scan_id() << '\\n';\n    return EXIT_SUCCESS;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. Operational Topology\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph Service Mesh (Istio)\n        SC[SecurityScanner] <-- gRPC/mTLS --> MN[MetricsNode]\n        SC <-- gRPC/mTLS --> BN[BackupNode]\n        SC <-- gRPC/mTLS --> AB[AlertBroker]\n    end\n    classDef svc fill:#0f5e9c,stroke:#fff,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff;\n    class SC,MN,BN,AB svc;\n```\n\nEnvoy sidecars transparently enforce per-method time-outs, automatic retries (`retryOn:\n5xx,connect-failure,refused-stream`) and distributed traces exported to the\nOpenTelemetry Collector.\n\n---\n\n### 6. Risk Mitigation & Future Work  \n\n* Blue-green roll-outs validated in a staging mesh before prod promotion.  \n* Pen-tests scheduled to validate certificate rotation and downgrade attack resilience.  \n* Evaluate HTTP/3 + gQUIC once officially supported by gRPC-C++.  \n\n---\n\n### 7. Rejected Alternatives\n\n| Alternative | Rationale for Rejection |\n|-------------|-------------------------|\n| Continue with REST/JSON + Custom TLS | Latency & missing streaming semantics outweighed familiarity benefits. |\n| Apache Thrift | We already depend on gRPC in the Java pipeline; doubling infra was unjustified. |\n| ZeroMQ | Lack of built-in authN/Z, difficult to operate at scale in Kubernetes. |\n\n---\n\nThis ADR is **accepted** and effective immediately.  All new internal service\ninterfaces **must** be defined in Protobuf and exposed via gRPC; legacy endpoints\nare slated for migration over the next two quarters.\n```",

  void set(const std::string& key, T&& value)\n    {\n        std::unique_lock lock(m_);\n        data_[key] = std::any(std::forward<T>(value));\n    }\n\n    template <typename T>\n    T get(const std::string& key) const\n    {\n        std::shared_lock lock(m_);\n        const auto it = data_.find(key);\n        if (it == data_.end())\n        {\n            throw std::out_of_range(\"CommandContext: key '\" + key + \"' not found.\");\n        }\n        return std::any_cast<T>(it->second);\n    }\n\n    bool contains(const std::string& key) const\n    {\n        std::shared_lock lock(m_);\n        return data_.count(key) > 0;\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    std::shared_ptr<ICommand>              command_;\n    std::unordered_map<std::string, std::any> data_;\n    mutable std::shared_mutex              m_;\n};\n\n/**\n * Single step in the validation/authorization/throttling pipeline.\n *\n * Implementations SHOULD:\n *   \u2022 Return `false` to short-circuit std::shared_ptr<ICommandMiddleware>;\n\n//---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// CommandHandler \u2014 heart of the orchestration layer\n//---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/**\n * Thread-safe, pluggable dispatcher that receives high-level commands and routes\n * them through middleware and into their concrete executors.\n *\n * Typical usage:\n *   auto handler = std::make_shared<CommandHandler>();\n *   handler->RegisterMiddleware(std::make_shared<AuthZMiddleware>());\n *   handler->RegisterExecutor<InitiateSecurityScanCmd>([](auto cmd, auto& ctx) { ... });\n *   handler->DispatchAsync(std::make_shared<InitiateSecurityScanCmd>(...));\n */\nclass CommandHandler : public std::enable_shared_from_this<CommandHandler>\n{\npublic:\n    CommandHandler()  = default;\n    ~CommandHandler() = default;\n    CommandHandler(const CommandHandler&)            = delete;\n    CommandHandler& operator=(const CommandHandler&) = delete;\n\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Executor registration\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    template <typename CommandT>\n    using ExecutorFunc = std::function<CommandResult(const std::shared_ptr<CommandT>&, CommandContext&)>;\n\n    /**\n     * Registers a concrete executor for a given Command-type.\n     * Thread-safe and idempotent per CommandT.\n     *\n     * Throws: std::logic_error when an executor is already registered.\n     */\n    template <typename CommandT>\n    void RegisterExecutor(ExecutorFunc<CommandT> executor);\n\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Middleware registration\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    void RegisterMiddleware(MiddlewarePtr middleware);\n\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Dispatch APIs\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    [[nodiscard]]\n    CommandResult Dispatch(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& command);\n\n    [[nodiscard]]\n    std::future<CommandResult> DispatchAsync(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& command);\n\nprivate:\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Internal type erasure for executors\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    struct IExecutorWrapper\n    {\n        virtual ~IExecutorWrapper() = default;\n        virtual CommandResult Execute(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& cmd,\n                                      CommandContext&                  ctx) = 0;\n    };\n\n    template <typename CommandT>\n    struct ExecutorWrapper final : IExecutorWrapper\n    {\n        explicit ExecutorWrapper(ExecutorFunc<CommandT> fn)\n            : fn_(std::move(fn))\n        {}\n\n        CommandResult Execute(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& cmd,\n                              CommandContext&                  ctx) override\n        {\n            auto concrete = std::dynamic_pointer_cast<CommandT>(cmd);\n            if (!concrete)\n                throw std::bad_cast();\n\n            return fn_(concrete, ctx);\n        }\n\n        ExecutorFunc<CommandT> fn_;\n    };\n\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Data members\n    //---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    std::unordered_map<std::type_index, std::shared_ptr<IExecutorWrapper>> executors_;\n    std::vector<MiddlewarePtr>                                             middleware_pipeline_;\n    mutable std::mutex                                                     m_;\n};\n\n//=====================================================================================================================\n//  Implementation  (header-only for ease of integration)\n//=====================================================================================================================\n\ntemplate <typename CommandT>\nvoid CommandHandler::RegisterExecutor(ExecutorFunc<CommandT> executor)\n{\n    if (!executor)\n        throw std::invalid_argument(\"CommandHandler::RegisterExecutor \u2013 executor is nullptr.\");\n\n    std::lock_guard lock(m_);\n    const std::type_index key(typeid(CommandT));\n\n    if (executors_.contains(key))\n        throw std::logic_error(\"CommandHandler::RegisterExecutor \u2013 executor already registered.\");\n\n    executors_[key] = std::make_shared<ExecutorWrapper<CommandT>>(std::move(executor));\n\n    FL360_LOG_INFO(\"Executor registered for command type: {}\", key.name());\n}\n\ninline void CommandHandler::RegisterMiddleware(MiddlewarePtr middleware)\n{\n    if (!middleware)\n        throw std::invalid_argument(\"CommandHandler::RegisterMiddleware \u2013 middleware is nullptr.\");\n\n    std::lock_guard lock(m_);\n    middleware_pipeline_.push_back(std::move(middleware));\n}\n\ninline CommandResult CommandHandler::Dispatch(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& command)\n{\n    if (!command)\n        throw std::invalid_argument(\"CommandHandler::Dispatch \u2013 command is nullptr.\");\n\n    CommandContext ctx(command);\n\n    // 1) Chain-of-Responsibility: middleware pipeline\n    for (const auto& mw : middleware_pipeline_)\n    {\n        bool proceed = false;\n        try\n        {\n            proceed = mw->Handle(ctx);\n        }\n        catch (const std::exception& ex)\n        {\n            FL360_LOG_ERROR(\"Middleware [{}] threw exception: {}\", typeid(*mw).name(), ex.what());\n            return { CommandStatus::Failed, ex.what() };\n        }\n\n        if (!proceed)\n        {\n            return { CommandStatus::Failed, \"Middleware aborted execution.\" };\n        }\n    }\n\n    // 2) Locate executor\n    std::shared_ptr<IExecutorWrapper> executor;\n    {\n        std::lock_guard lock(m_);\n        const std::type_index key(typeid(*command));\n        const auto            it = executors_.find(key);\n        if (it == executors_.end())\n        {\n            return { CommandStatus::Failed,\n                     \"No executor registered for command type: \" + std::string(key.name()) };\n        }\n        executor = it->second;\n    }\n\n    // 3) Execute\n    try\n    {\n        return executor->Execute(command, ctx);\n    }\n    catch (const std::exception& ex)\n    {\n        FL360_LOG_ERROR(\"Executor for [{}] threw exception: {}\", command->name(), ex.what());\n        return { CommandStatus::Failed, ex.what() };\n    }\n}\n\ninline std::future<CommandResult> CommandHandler::DispatchAsync(const std::shared_ptr<ICommand>& command)\n{\n    // The captured shared_ptr (self) guarantees the handler's lifetime for the async task.\n    auto self = shared_from_this();\n    return std::async(std::launch::async, [self, command] { return self->Dispatch(command); });\n}\n\n} // namespace fortiledger::orchestration\n```",

i < uuid.size(); ++i)\n        {\n            switch (i)\n            {\n                case 8: case 13: case 18: case 23:\n                    uuid[i] = '-';\n                    break;\n                case 14:\n                    uuid[i] = '4'; In production use <random> or\n        // OS-supplied CSPRNG for cryptographic quality.\n        thread_local uint32_t state =\n            static_cast<uint32_t>(std::chrono::high_resolution_clock::now()\n                                      .time_since_epoch()\n                                      .count());\n        state = state * 1664525u + 1013904223u;\n        return static_cast<int>((state >> 24) & 0xFF);\n    }\n\n    // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Observer helpers\n    // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n    void notifyObservers(const Result& r)\n    {\n        for (auto& obs : observers_) {\n            if (obs) { obs(*this, r); }\n        }\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    ScanContext                             context_;\n    std::shared_ptr<infra::IEventBus>       bus_;\n    std::vector<Observer>                   observers_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fortiledger360::domain::commands\n\n#endif  // FORTILEDGER360_DOMAIN_COMMANDS_SCAN_COMMAND_H",

YAML/JSON at runtime.            */\n    struct Config\n    {\n        std::chrono::milliseconds defaultTimeout  {std::chrono::seconds(30)};\n        double                    pricePerDeepScan{0.25};  // USD\n        double                    pricePerLightScan{0.10}; // USD\n        std::size_t               maxConcurrentScans {4};\n    };\n\n    /*  Callback that bills the tenant once the scan completes.           */\n    using BillingCallback =\n        std::function<void (const std::string& tenantId, double amount)>;\n\n    explicit PayGScanStrategy(\n            Config                       cfg           = {},\n            BillingCallback              billCb        = nullptr)\n        : config_(cfg)\n        , billingCb_(std::move(billCb))\n        , shutdown_{false}\n    {\n        spawnWorkers(config_.maxConcurrentScans);\n    }\n\n    PayGScanStrategy(const PayGScanStrategy&)            = delete;\n    PayGScanStrategy& operator=(const PayGScanStrategy&) = delete;\n    PayGScanStrategy(PayGScanStrategy&&)                 = delete;\n    PayGScanStrategy& operator=(PayGScanStrategy&&)      = delete;\n\n    ~PayGScanStrategy() override\n    {\n        /* Graceful shutdown \u2013 notify workers, then join. */\n        {\n            std::lock_guard lock(queueMtx_);\n            shutdown_ = true;\n        }\n        queueCv_.notify_all();\n        for (auto &t : workers_) { if (t.joinable()) t.join(); }\n    }\n\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    /*  SecurityScanStrategy API                                         */\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    [[nodiscard]] std::string id() const override\n    {\n        return \"PAYG_SCANNER_V1\";\n    }\n\n    std::string enqueueScan(const ScanRequest& request) override\n    {\n        /* Generate a deterministic UUID-like correlation id. */\n        const auto cid = generateCorrelationId();\n\n        {\n            std::lock_guard lock(queueMtx_);\n            if (shutdown_)\n                throw std::runtime_error(\n                        \"Cannot enqueue scan: strategy shutting down.\");\n            pending_.emplace(QueueItem{cid, request});\n        }\n        queueCv_.notify_one();\n        return cid;\n    }\n\n    std::optional<ScanResult>\n    pollResult(const std::string& correlationId) override\n    {\n        std::lock_guard lock(resultMtx_);\n        if (auto it = completed_.find(correlationId);\n            it != completed_.end())\n        {\n            auto result = std::move(it->second);\n            completed_.erase(it);\n            return result;\n        }\n        return std::nullopt;\n    }\n\n    void cancelScan(const std::string& correlationId) override\n    {\n        {\n            /* Quick pass \u2013 remove from pending queue if not yet started. */\n            std::lock_guard lock(queueMtx_);\n            if (cancelPendingLocked(correlationId))\n            {\n                return; // Already removed & notified observers.\n            }\n        }\n\n        /* If already running, flag it for cancellation. */\n        std::lock_guard lock(cancelMtx_);\n        cancelled_.insert(correlationId);\n    }\n\n    void registerObserver(ScanObserver observer) override\n    {\n        std::lock_guard lock(obsMtx_);\n        observers_.push_back(std::move(observer));\n    }\n\nprivate:\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    /*  Internal Queue/Threading                                         */\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    struct QueueItem\n    {\n        std::string correlationId;\n        ScanRequest request;\n\n        /* Highest priority first \u2013 normal > high => comparator reversed. */\n        bool operator<(const QueueItem& rhs) const noexcept\n        {\n            return static_cast<int>(request.priority) <\n                   static_cast<int>(rhs.request.priority);\n        }\n    };\n\n    void spawnWorkers(std::size_t poolSize)\n    {\n        for (std::size_t i = 0; i < poolSize; ++i)\n        {\n            workers_.emplace_back([this] { workerLoop(); });\n        }\n    }\n\n    void workerLoop()\n    {\n        while (true)\n        {\n            QueueItem item;\n            {\n                std::unique_lock lock(queueMtx_);\n                queueCv_.wait(lock, [this]\n                {\n                    return shutdown_ || !pending_.empty();\n                });\n\n                if (shutdown_ && pending_.empty())\n                    break;\n\n                item = pending_.top();\n                pending_.pop();\n            }\n\n            executeScan(item);\n        }\n    }\n\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    /*  Scan Execution Logic                                              */\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    void executeScan(const QueueItem& item)\n    {\n        const auto startedAt = std::chrono::steady_clock::now();\n        ScanResult result;\n        result.correlationId = item.correlationId;\n        result.tenantId      = item.request.tenantId;\n        result.assetId       = item.request.assetId;\n        result.state         = ScanState::Running;\n\n        /*  Simulated long-running scan; we simply sleep for demo.        */\n        const auto simulatedDuration =\n            item.request.deepScan ? std::chrono::seconds(5)\n                                  : std::chrono::seconds(2);\n\n        auto sleepUntil       = std::chrono::steady_clock::now()\n                              + simulatedDuration;\n        bool wasCancelled     = false;\n\n        while (std::chrono::steady_clock::now() < sleepUntil)\n        {\n            {\n                std::lock_guard lock(cancelMtx_);\n                if (cancelled_.erase(item.correlationId) > 0)\n                {\n                    wasCancelled = true;\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            std::this_thread::sleep_for(std::chrono::milliseconds(100));\n        }\n\n        /* Populate result. */\n        result.duration = std::chrono::duration_cast<std::chrono::milliseconds>(\n            std::chrono::steady_clock::now() - startedAt);\n\n        if (wasCancelled)\n        {\n            result.state = ScanState::Cancelled;\n            result.errorMessage = \"Scan cancelled by user.\";\n        }\n        else\n        {\n            /* 50/50 chance of \u201cfailure\u201d to illustrate states. */\n            if (randomBool(0.1))\n            {\n                result.state = ScanState::Failed;\n                result.errorMessage = \"Simulated vulnerability scan error.\";\n            }\n            else\n            {\n                result.state = ScanState::Succeeded;\n            }\n        }\n\n        /* Store into completed map for polling. */\n        {\n            std::lock_guard lock(resultMtx_);\n            completed_.emplace(result.correlationId, result);\n        }\n\n        /* Trigger billing if applicable and succeeded. */\n        if (billingCb_ && result.state == ScanState::Succeeded)\n        {\n            const double amount =\n                item.request.deepScan ? config_.pricePerDeepScan\n                                      : config_.pricePerLightScan;\n            billingCb_(result.tenantId, amount);\n        }\n\n        /* Notify observers \u2013 executed outside locks. */\n        notifyObservers(result);\n    }\n\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    /*  Utilities                                                         */\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    static std::string generateCorrelationId()\n    {\n        thread_local std::mt19937_64 rng{std::random_device{}()};\n        std::uniform_int_distribution<std::uint64_t> dist;\n        std::uint64_t part1 = dist(rng);\n        std::uint64_t part2 = dist(rng);\n        char buffer[33];\n        std::snprintf(buffer, sizeof(buffer), \"%016llx%016llx\",\n                      static_cast<unsigned long long>(part1),\n                      static_cast<unsigned long long>(part2));\n        return {buffer, 32};\n    }\n\n    static bool randomBool(double trueProbability = 0.5)\n    {\n        thread_local std::mt19937 rng{std::random_device{}()};\n        std::bernoulli_distribution dist{trueProbability};\n        return dist(rng);\n    }\n\n    bool cancelPendingLocked(const std::string& correlationId)\n    {\n        /* Because std::priority_queue offers no iterator, rebuild pile. */\n        std::priority_queue<QueueItem> newQueue;\n        bool found = false;\n\n        while (!pending_.empty())\n        {\n            auto item = pending_.top();\n            pending_.pop();\n\n            if (item.correlationId == correlationId)\n            {\n                /* Create immediate cancellation result. */\n                ScanResult result;\n                result.correlationId = item.correlationId;\n                result.tenantId      = item.request.tenantId;\n                result.assetId       = item.request.assetId;\n                result.state         = ScanState::Cancelled;\n                result.errorMessage  = \"Scan cancelled before execution.\";\n                result.duration      = std::chrono::milliseconds{0};\n\n                {\n                    std::lock_guard lock(resultMtx_);\n                    completed_.emplace(result.correlationId, result);\n                }\n\n                notifyObservers(result);\n                found = true;\n                continue;\n            }\n            newQueue.push(std::move(item));\n        }\n        std::swap(pending_, newQueue);\n        return found;\n    }\n\n    void notifyObservers(const ScanResult& result)\n    {\n        std::vector<ScanObserver> snapshot;\n        {\n            std::lock_guard lock(obsMtx_);\n            snapshot = observers_;\n        }\n        for (auto& obs : snapshot)\n        {\n            try\n            {\n                obs(result);\n            }\n            catch (...)\n            {\n                /* Observer must never crash the domain process. */\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    /*  Member Data                                                       */\n    /*-------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n    Config                    config_;\n    BillingCallback           billingCb_;\n\n    /* Worker pool. */\n    std::vector<std::thread>  workers_;\n    std::atomic<bool>         shutdown_;\n\n    /* Pending queue (priority). */\n    std::priority_queue<QueueItem> pending_;\n    std::mutex                      queueMtx_;\n    std::condition_variable         queueCv_;\n\n    /* Completed map. */\n    std::unordered_map<std::string, ScanResult> completed_;\n    std::mutex                                 resultMtx_;\n\n    /* Cancellation bookkeeping. */\n    std::unordered_set<std::string> cancelled_;\n    std::mutex                      cancelMtx_;\n\n    /* Observers. */\n    std::vector<ScanObserver> observers_;\n    std::mutex                obsMtx_;\n};\n\n} // namespace fortiledger360::domain::strategies",

Whenever an error\n *      occurs after a successful billing reservation, a compensating action\n *      is triggered to roll back the reserved credits.\n *\n *  Build Notes:\n *      \u2022 generate_uuid4()\n    {\n        static thread_local std::mt19937_64 rng{ std::random_device{}() };\n\n        std::uniform_int_distribution<uint64_t> dist(0, std::numeric_limits<uint64_t>::max());\n        uint64_t high = dist(rng);\n        uint64_t low  = dist(rng);\n\n        // Set the UUID version/fmt bits (version 4, variant 1):\n        high &= 0xFFFFFFFFFFFF0FFFULL;\n        high |= 0x0000000000004000ULL;\n        low  &= 0x3FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFULL;\n        low  |= 0x8000000000000000ULL;\n\n        std::ostringstream oss;\n        oss << std::hex << std::setfill('0')\n            << PayGScanStrategy::initiateScan(const TenantContext& tenant,\n                                    const ScanRequest&  request,\n                                    const utils::CancellationToken& token)\n{\n    const auto now = std::chrono::system_clock::now();\n\n    /*  1. Validation\n     *  -------------------------------------------------- */\n    if (token.isCancellationRequested())\n        throw std::runtime_error(\"Scan was cancelled before it started.\");\n\n    if (!tenant.isActive())\n        throw std::runtime_error(\"Inactive tenant.\");\n\n    if (!request.validate())\n        throw std::invalid_argument(\"ScanRequest validation error.\");\n\n    /*  2. cap      = 2s;\n    auto delay          = base * (1ULL << attempt);\n    if (delay > cap) delay = cap;\n\n    std::this_thread::sleep_for(delay);\n}\n\n/* ----------  EventPublisher public fa\u00e7ade The consumer is responsible for:\n *\n *       \u2022 Subscribing to a configurable list of topics\n *       \u2022 Gracefully handling rebalance events (partition assignment / revocation)\n *       \u2022 Deserializing JSON payloads into strongly-typed domain events\n *       \u2022 Delegating event execution to pluggable, run-time-bound dispatchers\n *       \u2022 Health monitoring, metrics collection, and structured logging\n *\n *  Design notes:\n *      \u2022 cppkafka is leveraged for Kafka integration       (https://github.com/mfontanini/cppkafka)\n *      \u2022 spdlog  is leveraged for structured logging       (https://github.com/gabime/spdlog)\n *      \u2022 nlohmann/json is used for lightweight JSON parsing (https://github.com/nlohmann/json)\n *\n *  License:\n *      Proprietary \u2014 FortiLedger360 (C) 2024.                     // \"kafka01:9092,kafka02:9092\"\n    std::string consumerGroup;               // \"scanner-service-v2\"\n    std::vector<std::string> topics;         // { \"security.scans\", \"invoices\" }\n    std::chrono::milliseconds pollTimeout{ 500 };\n    std::chrono::milliseconds metricsFlush{ 5'000 };\n    bool enableAutoCommit{ false };\n    size_t maxProcessingThreads{ std::thread::hardware_concurrency() };\n};\n\n//--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//  EventConsumer\n//--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nclass EventConsumer {\npublic:\n    EventConsumer(EventConsumerConfig config,\n                  std::shared_ptr<IEventDispatcher> dispatcher);\n\n    ~EventConsumer();\n\n    EventConsumer(const EventConsumer&)            = delete;\n    EventConsumer& operator=(const EventConsumer&) = delete;\n    EventConsumer(EventConsumer&&)                 = delete;\n    EventConsumer& operator=(EventConsumer&&)      = delete;\n\n    /**\n     * Begins the consumption loop (non-blocking).\n     */\n    void start();\n\n    /**\n     * Request a graceful shutdown.  Blocks until the internal thread terminates.\n     */\n    void stop();\n\n    /**\n     * Returns true while the consumer loop is running.\n     */\n    bool isRunning() const noexcept;\n\nprivate:\n Implementation\n//--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nstatic std::shared_ptr<spdlog::logger> createDefaultLogger(const std::string& consumerGroup) {\n    auto logger = spdlog::stdout_color_mt(\"event_consumer:\" + consumerGroup);\n    logger->set_pattern(\"[%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%e] [%^%l%$] %v\");\n    return EventConsumerException(\"EventConsumer requires a non-null IEventDispatcher.\");\n    }\n    // Attach rebalance callback for detailed diagnostics\n    consumer_.set_assignment_callback([this](const EventConsumer::start() {\n    if (running_.exchange(true)) {\n        log_->warn(\"EventConsumer already running\");\n        return;\n    }\n    worker_ = std::thread(&EventConsumer::consumeLoop, started (pollTimeout={}ms)\",\n               config_.pollTimeout.count());\n\n    // Thread pool for event processing\n    std::vector<std::thread> processingThreads;\n    std::mutex               queueMutex;\n    std::condition_variable  queueCond;\n    std::deque<cppkafka::Message> messageQueue;\n    std::atomic<bool>        processingStop{ false };\n\n    // Worker lambda\n    auto workerFn
